<th scope="row">Battles/wars</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a></td>

<p><b>Benjamin Harrison</b> (August 20, 1833&#160;– March 13, 1901) was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States" title="List of Presidents of the United States">23rd</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a> (1889–1893); he was the grandson of the ninth President, <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Harrison" title="William Henry Harrison">William Henry Harrison</a>. Before ascending to the presidency, Harrison established himself as a prominent local attorney, Presbyterian church leader and politician in <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">Indianapolis</a>, Indiana. During the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, he served the Union as a <a href="/wiki/Colonel_(United_States)" title="Colonel (United States)">colonel</a> and on February 14, 1865 was confirmed by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">U.S. Senate</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Brevet_(military)" title="Brevet (military)">brevet</a> <a href="/wiki/Brigadier_general_(United_States)" title="Brigadier general (United States)">brigadier general</a> of volunteers to rank from January 23, 1865. After the war, he unsuccessfully ran for the governorship of <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>. He was later elected to the U.S. Senate by the Indiana legislature.</p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>, Harrison was elected to the presidency in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1888" title="United States presidential election, 1888">1888</a>, defeating the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> incumbent <a href="/wiki/Grover_Cleveland" title="Grover Cleveland">Grover Cleveland</a>. Hallmarks of his administration included unprecedented economic legislation, including the <a href="/wiki/McKinley_Tariff" title="McKinley Tariff">McKinley Tariff</a>, which imposed historic protective trade rates, and the <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Antitrust_Act" title="Sherman Antitrust Act">Sherman Antitrust Act</a>; Harrison facilitated the creation of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Forest" title="United States National Forest">National Forests</a> through an amendment to the Land Revision Act of 1891. He also substantially strengthened and modernized the Navy, and conducted an active foreign policy. He proposed, in vain, federal education funding as well as voting rights enforcement for <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans" class="mw-redirect">African Americans</a> during his administration.</p>
<p>Due in large part to surplus revenues from the tariffs, federal spending reached one billion dollars for the first time during his term. The spending issue in part led to the defeat of the Republicans in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_election,_1890" title="United States House election, 1890" class="mw-redirect">1890 mid-term elections</a>. Harrison was defeated by Cleveland in his bid for re-election in 1892, due to the growing unpopularity of the high tariff and high federal spending. He then returned to private life in Indianapolis but later represented the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venezuela" title="Republic of Venezuela" class="mw-redirect">Republic of Venezuela</a> in an international case against the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a>. In 1900, he traveled to Europe as part of the case and, after a brief stay, returned to Indianapolis. He died the following year of complications from <a href="/wiki/Influenza" title="Influenza">influenza</a>. Although many have praised Harrison's commitment to African Americans' voting rights, scholars and historians generally regard his administration as below-average, and <a href="/wiki/Historical_rankings_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States" title="Historical rankings of Presidents of the United States">rank him in the bottom half</a> among U.S. presidents.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family_and_education">Family and education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Family and education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Harrison's paternal ancestors were the <a href="/wiki/Harrison_family_of_Virginia" title="Harrison family of Virginia">Virginia Harrisons</a>. Their immigrant ancestor was Benjamin Harrison, who arrived in <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">Jamestown, Virginia</a>, in 1630. The future president Benjamin was born on August 20, 1833, in <a href="/wiki/North_Bend,_Ohio" title="North Bend, Ohio">North Bend</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a>, as the second of eight children to <a href="/wiki/John_Scott_Harrison" title="John Scott Harrison">John Scott Harrison</a> and Elizabeth Ramsey (Irwin). Benjamin was a grandson of President William Henry Harrison and the great-grandson of <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Harrison_V" title="Benjamin Harrison V">Benjamin Harrison V</a>, a Virginia governor and signer of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun7.E2.80.938Moore_.26_Hale15_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun7.E2.80.938Moore_.26_Hale15-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-VIII_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VIII-2"><span>[</span>a<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison was seven years old when his grandfather was elected President, but he did not attend the inauguration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun8_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun8-3"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Although Harrison's family was distinguished, his parents were not wealthy. John Scott Harrison spent much of his farm income on his children's education.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun9Sieversv._1.2C_pp._21.E2.80.9323_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun9Sieversv._1.2C_pp._21.E2.80.9323-4"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite the family's meager resources, Harrison's boyhood was enjoyable, much of it spent outdoors fishing or hunting.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESievers22.E2.80.9323v._1_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESievers22.E2.80.9323v._1-5"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Benjamin Harrison's early schooling took place in a one-room schoolhouse near his home, but his parents later arranged for a tutor to help him with college preparatory studies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESievers24.E2.80.9329v._1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESievers24.E2.80.9329v._1-6"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison and his brother Irwin enrolled in <a href="/wiki/Farmer%27s_College" title="Farmer's College" class="mw-redirect">Farmer's College</a> near Cincinnati, Ohio in 1847.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESievers29.E2.80.9330v._1_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESievers29.E2.80.9330v._1-7"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> He attended the college for two years <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWallace53_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWallace53-8"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Farmer.27s_College_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Farmer.27s_College-9"><span>[</span>b<span>]</span></a></sup> and while there met his future wife, <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Harrison" title="Caroline Harrison">Caroline Lavinia Scott</a>, one of the daughters of the science professor, <a href="/wiki/John_Witherspoon_Scott" title="John Witherspoon Scott">John Witherspoon Scott</a>.</p>
<p>In 1850, Harrison transferred to <a href="/wiki/Miami_University" title="Miami University">Miami University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Oxford,_Ohio" title="Oxford, Ohio">Oxford, Ohio</a> and graduated in 1852.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale21.E2.80.9323Sieversv._1.2C_p._58_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale21.E2.80.9323Sieversv._1.2C_p._58-10"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> He joined the fraternity <a href="/wiki/Phi_Delta_Theta" title="Phi Delta Theta">Phi Delta Theta</a>, which he used as a network for much of his life. He was also a member of <a href="/wiki/Delta_Chi" title="Delta Chi">Delta Chi</a>, a law fraternity which permitted dual membership.<sup id="cite_ref-fraternities_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fraternities-11"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Classmates included <a href="/wiki/John_Alexander_Anderson" title="John Alexander Anderson">John Alexander Anderson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun23_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun23-12"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> who became a six-term congressman, and <a href="/wiki/Whitelaw_Reid" title="Whitelaw Reid">Whitelaw Reid</a> who ran as Harrison's vice presidential candidate in his presidential reelection campaign. At Miami, Harrison was strongly influenced by history and political economy professor <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hamilton_Bishop" title="Robert Hamilton Bishop">Robert Hamilton Bishop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun10.E2.80.9311Sieversv._1.2C_pp._31.E2.80.9334_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun10.E2.80.9311Sieversv._1.2C_pp._31.E2.80.9334-13"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison joined a <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian" title="Presbyterian" class="mw-redirect">Presbyterian</a> church at college and, like his mother, became a lifelong member.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWallace58_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWallace58-14"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After completing college, Harrison took up the study of law as a legal apprentice in the Cincinnati law office of Storer &amp; Gwynne.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage.2C_family_and_early_career">Marriage, family and early career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Marriage, family and early career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Benjamin_Harrison_c1850.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Benjamin_Harrison_c1850.jpg/220px-Benjamin_Harrison_c1850.jpg" width="220" height="268" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Benjamin_Harrison_c1850.jpg/330px-Benjamin_Harrison_c1850.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Benjamin_Harrison_c1850.jpg/440px-Benjamin_Harrison_c1850.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1831" data-file-height="2232" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Benjamin_Harrison_c1850.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Benjamin Harrison c1850</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Before completing his law studies, Harrison returned to Oxford to marry Caroline Scott.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun11.E2.80.9312.2C_23_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun11.E2.80.9312.2C_23-15"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> On October 20, 1853, Caroline's father, also a Presbyterian minister, performed the ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun23_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun23-12"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Harrisons had two children, <a href="/wiki/Russell_Benjamin_Harrison" title="Russell Benjamin Harrison">Russell Benjamin Harrison</a> (August 12, 1854&#160;– December 13, 1936), and <a href="/wiki/Mary_Harrison_McKee" title="Mary Harrison McKee">Mary "Mamie" Scott Harrison</a> (April 3, 1858&#160;– October 28, 1930).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun27_.26_29_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun27_.26_29-16"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Harrison returned to live on his father's farm while finishing his law studies. That same year, he inherited $800 after the death of an aunt, and used the funds to move with Caroline to Indianapolis, Indiana in 1854.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun26_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun26-17"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> He was admitted to the bar and began practicing law in the office of John H. Ray. The same year he became a <a href="/wiki/Town_crier" title="Town crier">crier</a> for the Federal Court in Indianapolis, for which he was paid $2.50 per day.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun27_.26_29_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun27_.26_29-16"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison became a founding member and first president of both the University Club, a private <a href="/wiki/Gentlemen%27s_club" title="Gentlemen's club">gentlemen's club</a> and the Phi Delta Theta Alumni Club.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun22_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun22-18"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison and his wife joined and assumed leadership positions at the First Presbyterian Church.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter7_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter7-19"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Having grown up in a <a href="/wiki/Whig_party_(United_States)" title="Whig party (United States)" class="mw-redirect">Whig</a> household, he favored that party's politics while young. He joined the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Republican_Party" title="United States Republican Party" class="mw-redirect">Republican Party</a> shortly after its formation in 1856, and that year campaigned on behalf of the Republican presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/John_C._Fr%C3%A9mont" title="John C. Frémont">John C. Frémont</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun18_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun18-20"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison was elected as the Indianapolis City Attorney that year, a position that paid an annual salary of $400.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale29_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale29-21"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1858, Harrison entered into a law partnership with William Wallace and they opened their office called Wallace &amp; Harrison.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun28Sieversv._1.2C_p._105_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun28Sieversv._1.2C_p._105-22"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> In Two years hence, Harrison successfully ran as the Republican candidate for <a href="/wiki/Reporter_of_decisions" title="Reporter of decisions">reporter</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Indiana_Supreme_Court" title="Indiana Supreme Court" class="mw-redirect">Indiana Supreme Court</a>. He was an active supporter of his party's platform, and served as Republican State Committee Secretary. His law partner Wallace was elected as county clerk in 1860; Harrison established a new firm with William Fishback, named Fishback &amp; Harrison. They worked together until he entered the Army after the start of the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESievers171v._1_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESievers171v._1-23"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War">Civil War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Civil War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:General-Benjamin-Harrison-in-uniform,-1865.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/General-Benjamin-Harrison-in-uniform%2C-1865.jpg/170px-General-Benjamin-Harrison-in-uniform%2C-1865.jpg" width="170" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/General-Benjamin-Harrison-in-uniform%2C-1865.jpg/255px-General-Benjamin-Harrison-in-uniform%2C-1865.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/General-Benjamin-Harrison-in-uniform%2C-1865.jpg/340px-General-Benjamin-Harrison-in-uniform%2C-1865.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1301" data-file-height="1769" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:General-Benjamin-Harrison-in-uniform,-1865.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brigadier General Harrison (left) with other commanders of the XX Corps, 1865</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1862, <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a> issued a call for more recruits for the Union Army; Harrison wanted to enlist, but worried about how to support his young family.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun20_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun20-24"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> While visiting Governor <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Morton" title="Oliver Morton" class="mw-redirect">Oliver Morton</a>, Harrison found him distressed over the shortage of men answering the latest call. Harrison told the governor, "If I can be of any service, I will go".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWallace180Calhoun34_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWallace180Calhoun34-25"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Morton asked Harrison if he could help recruit a regiment, although he would not ask him to serve. Harrison recruited throughout northern Indiana to raise a regiment. Morton offered him the command, but Harrison declined, as he had no military experience. He was initially commissioned as a captain and company commander on July 22, 1862. Governor Morton commissioned Harrison as a colonel on August 7, 1862, and the newly formed <a href="/wiki/70th_Indiana_Infantry_Regiment" title="70th Indiana Infantry Regiment">70th Indiana</a> was mustered into Federal service on August 12, 1862. Once mustered, the regiment left Indiana to join the Union Army at Louisville, Kentucky.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWallace180.E2.80.93181Calhoun21.E2.80.9323.2C_41.2C_44_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWallace180.E2.80.93181Calhoun21.E2.80.9323.2C_41.2C_44-26"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>For much of its first two years, the 70th Indiana performed reconnaissance duty and guarded railroads in <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>. In 1864, Harrison and his regiment joined <a href="/wiki/William_T._Sherman" title="William T. Sherman" class="mw-redirect">William T. Sherman</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Campaign" title="Atlanta Campaign">Atlanta Campaign</a> and moved to the front lines. On January 2, 1864, Harrison was promoted to command the 1st Brigade of the 1st Division of the <a href="/wiki/XX_Corps_(Union_Army)" title="XX Corps (Union Army)">XX Corps</a>. He commanded the <a href="/wiki/Brigade" title="Brigade">brigade</a> at the battles of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Resaca" title="Battle of Resaca">Resaca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cassville,_Georgia" title="Cassville, Georgia">Cassville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_New_Hope_Church" title="Battle of New Hope Church">New Hope Church</a>, Lost Mountain, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kennesaw_Mountain" title="Battle of Kennesaw Mountain">Kennesaw Mountain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Marietta" title="Battle of Marietta">Marietta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Peachtree_Creek" title="Battle of Peachtree Creek">Peachtree Creek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Atlanta" title="Battle of Atlanta">Atlanta</a>. When Sherman's main force began its <a href="/wiki/Sherman%27s_March_to_the_Sea" title="Sherman's March to the Sea">March to the Sea</a>, Harrison's brigade was transferred to the District of Etowah and participated in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nashville" title="Battle of Nashville">Battle of Nashville</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun36.E2.80.9344Wallace209.E2.80.93225_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun36.E2.80.9344Wallace209.E2.80.93225-28"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On January 23, 1865, President Lincoln nominated Harrison to the grade of <a href="/wiki/Brevet_(military)" title="Brevet (military)">brevet</a> <a href="/wiki/Brigadier_general_(United_States)" title="Brigadier general (United States)">brigadier general</a> of volunteers, to rank from that date, and the Senate confirmed the nomination on February 14, 1865.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> He rode in the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Review_of_the_Armies" title="Grand Review of the Armies">Grand Review</a> in Washington, D.C. before mustering out on June 8, 1865.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun36.E2.80.9344Wallace209.E2.80.93225_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun36.E2.80.9344Wallace209.E2.80.93225-28"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_career">Post-war career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Post-war career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indiana_politics">Indiana politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Indiana politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While serving in the army in October 1864, Harrison was reelected <a href="/wiki/Law_report" title="Law report">reporter</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Indiana" title="Supreme Court of Indiana">Supreme Court of Indiana</a> and served four more years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun19_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun19-30"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> Although not politically powerful, the position provided Harrison a steady income.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun19_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun19-30"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> President <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_Simpson_Grant" title="Ulysses Simpson Grant" class="mw-redirect">Grant</a> appointed him to represent the federal government in a civil claim brought by <a href="/wiki/Lambdin_P._Milligan" title="Lambdin P. Milligan">Lambdin P. Milligan</a>, whose wartime conviction for <a href="/wiki/Treason" title="Treason">treason</a> had been reversed by the Supreme Court. Due to Harrison's advocacy, the damages awarded against the government were minimal.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWallace93.E2.80.9394.2C_119_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWallace93.E2.80.9394.2C_119-31"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>With his increasing reputation, local Republicans urged Harrison to run for Congress. He initially confined his political activities to speaking on behalf of other Republican candidates, a task for which he received high praises from his colleagues.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun27.E2.80.9328Socolofsky_.26_Spetter8_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun27.E2.80.9328Socolofsky_.26_Spetter8-32"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Benjamin_Harrison_Home.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Benjamin_Harrison_Home.jpg/220px-Benjamin_Harrison_Home.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Benjamin_Harrison_Home.jpg/330px-Benjamin_Harrison_Home.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Benjamin_Harrison_Home.jpg/440px-Benjamin_Harrison_Home.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4204" data-file-height="3137" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Benjamin_Harrison_Home.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Harrison_Home" title="Benjamin Harrison Home">Benjamin Harrison Home</a> in Indianapolis</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1872, Harrison campaigned for the Republican nomination for <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Indiana" title="Governor of Indiana">governor of Indiana</a>. Former governor Oliver Morton favored his opponent, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_M._Browne" title="Thomas M. Browne">Thomas M. Browne</a>, and Harrison lost his bid for statewide office.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale28_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale28-33"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> He returned to his law practice and, despite the <a href="/wiki/Panic_of_1873" title="Panic of 1873">Panic of 1873</a>, he was financially successful enough to build a grand new home in Indianapolis in 1874.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun29_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun29-34"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> He continued to make speeches on behalf of Republican candidates and policies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun30_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun30-35"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1876, the original Republican nominee for governor dropped out of the race and Harrison accepted the Republicans' invitation to take his place on the ticket.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun32Socolofsky_.26_Spetter8_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun32Socolofsky_.26_Spetter8-36"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> He centered his campaign on economic policy and favored deflating the national currency. He was ultimately defeated in a plurality by <a href="/wiki/James_D._Williams" title="James D. Williams">James D. Williams</a>, losing by 5,084 votes out of a total 434,457 cast.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWallace266Calhoun32_.26_58_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWallace266Calhoun32_.26_58-37"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> Following his defeat, Harrison was able to build on his new prominence in the state. When the <a href="/wiki/Great_Railroad_Strike_of_1877" title="Great Railroad Strike of 1877">Great Railroad Strike of 1877</a> reached Indianapolis, he helped to mediate between the workers and management and to preserve public order.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun33.E2.80.9334_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun33.E2.80.9334-38"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>When United States Senator Morton died in 1878, the Republicans nominated Harrison to run for the seat, but the party failed to gain a majority in the state legislature, which at that time elected senators; the Democratic majority elected <a href="/wiki/Daniel_W._Voorhees" title="Daniel W. Voorhees">Daniel W. Voorhees</a> instead.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun35.E2.80.9336_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun35.E2.80.9336-39"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Seventeenth_Amendment_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seventeenth_Amendment-40"><span>[</span>c<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1879 President <a href="/wiki/Rutherford_B._Hayes" title="Rutherford B. Hayes">Hayes</a> appointed Harrison to the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River_Commission" title="Mississippi River Commission" class="mw-redirect">Mississippi River Commission</a>, which worked to develop internal improvements on the river.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter8_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter8-41"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> As a delegate to the <a href="/wiki/1880_Republican_National_Convention" title="1880 Republican National Convention">1880 Republican National Convention</a> the following year,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun36_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun36-42"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> he was instrumental in breaking a deadlock on candidates, and <a href="/wiki/James_A._Garfield" title="James A. Garfield">James A. Garfield</a> won the nomination.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_Senator">United States Senator</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: United States Senator">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walter_Q._Gresham_-_Brady-Handy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Walter_Q._Gresham_-_Brady-Handy.jpg/170px-Walter_Q._Gresham_-_Brady-Handy.jpg" width="170" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Walter_Q._Gresham_-_Brady-Handy.jpg/255px-Walter_Q._Gresham_-_Brady-Handy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Walter_Q._Gresham_-_Brady-Handy.jpg/340px-Walter_Q._Gresham_-_Brady-Handy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3216" data-file-height="3848" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walter_Q._Gresham_-_Brady-Handy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Walter_Q._Gresham" title="Walter Q. Gresham">Walter Q. Gresham</a>, Harrison's rival within the Indiana Republican Party</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After Harrison led the Republican delegation at the National Convention, he was considered a presumptive Senate candidate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun37_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun37-43"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> He gave speeches in favor of Garfield in Indiana and New York, further raising his profile in the party. When the Republicans retook the <a href="/wiki/Indiana_General_Assembly" title="Indiana General Assembly">state legislature</a>, Harrison's election to the Senate was threatened by his intra-party rival Judge <a href="/wiki/Walter_Q._Gresham" title="Walter Q. Gresham">Walter Q. Gresham</a>, but Harrison was ultimately chosen.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun37_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun37-43"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> After Garfield's election as president in 1880, his administration offered Harrison a cabinet position which he declined in favor of continued service as senator. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun60Socolofsky_.26_Spetter8_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun60Socolofsky_.26_Spetter8-44"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Harrison served in the Senate from March 4, 1881, to March 4, 1887 and chaired the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Transportation_Routes_to_the_Seaboard" title="United States Senate Committee on Transportation Routes to the Seaboard">U.S. Senate Committee on Transportation Routes to the Seaboard</a> (<a href="/wiki/Forty-seventh_United_States_Congress" title="Forty-seventh United States Congress" class="mw-redirect">47th Congress</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Territories" title="United States Senate Committee on Territories" class="mw-redirect">U.S. Senate Committee on Territories</a> (<a href="/wiki/Forty-eighth_United_States_Congress" title="Forty-eighth United States Congress" class="mw-redirect">48th</a> and <a href="/wiki/Forty-ninth_United_States_Congress" title="Forty-ninth United States Congress" class="mw-redirect">49th Congresses</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWallace265.E2.80.93267Calhoun59_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWallace265.E2.80.93267Calhoun59-45"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1881, the major issue confronting Senator Harrison was the budget surplus. Democrats wished to reduce the <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariff</a> and limit the amount of money the government took in; Republicans instead wished to spend the money on <a href="/wiki/Internal_improvements" title="Internal improvements">internal improvements</a> and pensions for Civil War veterans. Harrison took his party's side and advocated for generous <a href="/wiki/Pension" title="Pension">pensions</a> for veterans and their widows.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun39_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun39-46"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> He also supported, unsuccessfully, aid for education of Southerners, especially the children of the freedmen; he believed that education was necessary to help the black population rise to political and economic equality with whites. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun39.E2.80.9340_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun39.E2.80.9340-47"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison opposed the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Exclusion_Act_(United_States)" title="Chinese Exclusion Act (United States)" class="mw-redirect">Chinese Exclusion Act of 1882</a>, which his party supported, as he thought it violated existing treaties with <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun40_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun40-48"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1884, Harrison and Gresham competed for influence at the <a href="/wiki/1884_Republican_National_Convention" title="1884 Republican National Convention">1884 Republican National Convention</a>.;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun41.E2.80.9342_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun41.E2.80.9342-49"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> the delegation ended up supporting <a href="/wiki/James_G._Blaine" title="James G. Blaine">James G. Blaine</a>, the eventual nominee.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun41.E2.80.9342_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun41.E2.80.9342-49"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> In the Senate, Harrison achieved passage of his Dependent Pension Bill, only to see it vetoed by President <a href="/wiki/Grover_Cleveland" title="Grover Cleveland">Grover Cleveland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun42_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun42-50"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> His efforts to further the admission of new western states were stymied by Democrats, who feared that the new states would elect Republicans to Congress.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun42_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun42-50"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1885, the Democrats <a href="/wiki/Redistricting" title="Redistricting">redistricted</a> the Indiana state legislature, which resulted in an increased Democratic majority in 1886, despite an overall Republican majority statewide.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun43.E2.80.9344_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun43.E2.80.9344-51"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison was thereby defeated in his bid for reelection; this resulted after a deadlock in the <a href="/wiki/Indiana_Senate" title="Indiana Senate">state senate</a>, with the legislature eventually choosing Democrat <a href="/wiki/David_Turpie" title="David Turpie">David Turpie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale66_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale66-52"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison then returned to Indianapolis and his law practice, but stayed active in state and national politics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun45.E2.80.9346_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun45.E2.80.9346-53"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Election_of_1888">Election of 1888</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Election of 1888">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1888" title="United States presidential election, 1888">United States presidential election, 1888</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harrison-Morton_1888.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Harrison-Morton_1888.jpg/220px-Harrison-Morton_1888.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Harrison-Morton_1888.jpg/330px-Harrison-Morton_1888.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Harrison-Morton_1888.jpg/440px-Harrison-Morton_1888.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="500" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harrison-Morton_1888.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Harrison–Morton campaign poster</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nomination">Nomination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Nomination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The initial favorite for the Republican nomination was the previous nominee, James G. Blaine of <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a>. After Blaine wrote several letters denying any interest in the nomination, his supporters divided among other candidates, with <a href="/wiki/John_Sherman_(politician)" title="John Sherman (politician)" class="mw-redirect">John Sherman</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a> as the leader among them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun47_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun47-54"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Others, including <a href="/wiki/Chauncey_Depew" title="Chauncey Depew">Chauncey Depew</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russell_Alger" title="Russell Alger" class="mw-redirect">Russell Alger</a> of <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>, and Harrison's old nemesis Walter Q. Gresham, now <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Seventh_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Seventh Circuit">a federal appellate court judge in Chicago</a>, also sought the delegates' support at the <a href="/wiki/1888_Republican_National_Convention" title="1888 Republican National Convention">1888 Republican National Convention</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun47_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun47-54"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Blaine did not publicly endorse any of the candidates as a successor; however, on March 1, 1888 he privately wrote that "the one man remaining who in my judgment can make the best one is Benjamin Harrison."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter8_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter8-41"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Harrison placed fourth on the first ballot, with Sherman in the lead, and the next few ballots showed little change.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun50_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun50-55"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> The Blaine supporters shifted their support among candidates they found acceptable, and when they shifted to Harrison, they found a candidate who could attract the votes of many other delegations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun51.E2.80.9352_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun51.E2.80.9352-56"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> He was nominated as the party's presidential candidate on the eighth ballot, by a count of 544 to 108 votes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWallace271_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWallace271-57"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Levi_P._Morton" title="Levi P. Morton">Levi P. Morton</a> of New York was chosen as his running mate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter9_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter9-58"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Election_over_Cleveland">Election over Cleveland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Election over Cleveland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ElectoralCollege1888.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/ElectoralCollege1888.svg/300px-ElectoralCollege1888.svg.png" width="300" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/ElectoralCollege1888.svg/450px-ElectoralCollege1888.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/ElectoralCollege1888.svg/600px-ElectoralCollege1888.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1020" data-file-height="593" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ElectoralCollege1888.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Results of the 1888 election</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Harrison's opponent in the general election was incumbent President Grover Cleveland. He reprised a more traditional <a href="/wiki/Front_porch_campaign" title="Front porch campaign">front-porch campaign</a>, abandoned by his immediate predecessors; he received visiting delegations to Indianapolis and made ninety plus pronouncements from his home town.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter11_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter11-59"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> The Republicans campaigned heavily in favor of <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">protective tariffs</a>, turning out protectionist voters in the important industrial states of the North. The election focused on the swing states of New York, New Jersey, Connecticut, and Harrison's home state of Indiana.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter10_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter10-60"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison and Cleveland split these four states, with Harrison winning in New York and Indiana.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun43Socolofsky_.26_Spetter13_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun43Socolofsky_.26_Spetter13-61"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> Voter turnout was 79.3%, reflecting a large interest in the campaign; nearly eleven million votes were cast.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun57_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun57-62"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Although Harrison received 90,000 fewer popular votes than Cleveland, he carried the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" title="Electoral College (United States)">Electoral College</a> 233 to 168.<sup id="cite_ref-EV_1888_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EV_1888-63"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> Allegations were made against Republicans for engaging in irregular ballot practices; an example was described as <a href="/wiki/Blocks_of_Five" title="Blocks of Five">Blocks of Five</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter13_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter13-64"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Although he had made no political bargains, his supporters had given many pledges upon his behalf. When Boss <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Quay" title="Matthew Quay">Matthew Quay</a> of Pennsylvania, who rebuffed for a Cabinet position for his political support during the convention, heard that Harrison ascribed his narrow victory to <a href="/wiki/Divine_Providence" title="Divine Providence" class="mw-redirect">Providence</a>, Quay exclaimed that Harrison would never know "how close a number of men were compelled to approach...the penitentiary to make him President."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun55.2C_60_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun55.2C_60-65"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison was known as the Centennial President because his inauguration celebrated the <a href="/wiki/George_Washington%27s_legacy#Centennial_celebration" title="George Washington's legacy">centenary of the first inauguration</a> of <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> in 1789.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun47.E2.80.9354_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun47.E2.80.9354-66"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> In congressional elections, the Republicans increased their membership in the House of Representatives by nineteen seats.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter14_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter14-67"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidency_1889.E2.80.931893">Presidency 1889–1893</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Presidency 1889–1893">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harrison-inauguration.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Harrison-inauguration.jpg/220px-Harrison-inauguration.jpg" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Harrison-inauguration.jpg/330px-Harrison-inauguration.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Harrison-inauguration.jpg/440px-Harrison-inauguration.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4173" data-file-height="3450" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harrison-inauguration.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Inauguration of Benjamin Harrison, March 4, 1889. Cleveland held Harrison's umbrella</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inauguration_and_cabinet">Inauguration and cabinet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Inauguration and cabinet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Harrison was sworn into office on Monday, March 4, 1889 by <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_the_United_States" title="Chief Justice of the United States">Chief Justice</a> <a href="/wiki/Melville_Fuller" title="Melville Fuller">Melville Fuller</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter1.E2.80.932_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter1.E2.80.932-68"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> At 5' 6" tall, he was only slightly taller than Madison, the shortest president, but much heavier; he was the fourth (and last) president to sport a full beard<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter1_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter1-69"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison's <a href="/wiki/Inauguration" title="Inauguration">Inauguration</a> ceremony took place during a <a href="/wiki/Rainstorm" title="Rainstorm" class="mw-redirect">rainstorm</a> in Washington D.C.. Outgoing U.S. President Grover Cleveland attended the ceremony and held an umbrella over Harrison's head as he took the oath of office.</p>
<p>His speech was brief – half as long as that of his grandfather, William Henry Harrison, whose speech holds the record for the longest inaugural address of a U.S. president.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter1.E2.80.932_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter1.E2.80.932-68"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> In his speech, Benjamin Harrison credited the nation's growth to the influences of education and religion, urged the cotton states and mining territories to attain the industrial proportions of the eastern states and promised a protective tariff. Concerning commerce, he said, "If our great corporations would more scrupulously observe their legal obligations and duties, they would have less call to complain of the limitations of their rights or of interference with their operations."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter3_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter3-70"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison also urged early statehood for the territories and advocated pensions for veterans, a statement that was met with enthusiastic applause. In foreign affairs, Harrison reaffirmed the <a href="/wiki/Monroe_Doctrine" title="Monroe Doctrine">Monroe Doctrine</a> as a mainstay of foreign policy, while urging modernization of the Navy and a merchant marine force. He gave his commitment to international peace through noninterference in the affairs of foreign governments.<sup id="cite_ref-Benjamin_Harrison_Inauguration_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benjamin_Harrison_Inauguration-71"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/John_Philip_Sousa" title="John Philip Sousa">John Philip Sousa</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps" title="Marine Corps" class="mw-redirect">Marine Corps</a> band played at the Inaugural Ball inside the <a href="/wiki/National_Building_Museum" title="National Building Museum">Pension Building</a> with a large crowd attending.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter5.E2.80.936_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter5.E2.80.936-72"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> After moving into the White House, Harrison noted, quite prophetically, "There is only a door – one that is never locked – between the president's office and what are not very accurately called his private apartments. There should be an executive office building, not too far away, but wholly distinct from the dwelling house. For everyone else in the public service there is an unroofed space between the bedroom and the desk."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter83_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter83-73"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width: 230px;">
<div style="width: 230px; height: 270px; overflow: hidden;">
<div style="position: relative; top: -50px; left: -50px; width: 325px"><a href="/wiki/File:HARRISON,_Benjamin-President_(BEP_engraved_portrait).jpg" class="image"><img alt="BEP engraved portrait of Harrison as President" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/HARRISON%2C_Benjamin-President_%28BEP_engraved_portrait%29.jpg/325px-HARRISON%2C_Benjamin-President_%28BEP_engraved_portrait%29.jpg" width="325" height="412" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/HARRISON%2C_Benjamin-President_%28BEP_engraved_portrait%29.jpg/488px-HARRISON%2C_Benjamin-President_%28BEP_engraved_portrait%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/HARRISON%2C_Benjamin-President_%28BEP_engraved_portrait%29.jpg/650px-HARRISON%2C_Benjamin-President_%28BEP_engraved_portrait%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="9000" data-file-height="11400" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HARRISON,_Benjamin-President_(BEP_engraved_portrait).jpg" title="File:HARRISON, Benjamin-President (BEP engraved portrait).jpg">File:HARRISON, Benjamin-President (BEP engraved portrait).jpg</a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Engraving_and_Printing" title="Bureau of Engraving and Printing">BEP</a> engraved portrait of Harrison as President</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Harrison acted quite independently in selecting his cabinet, much to the dismay of the Republican bosses. He began by delaying the presumed nomination of James G. Blaine as Secretary of State so as to preclude Blaine's involvement in the formation of the administration, as had occurred in President Garfield's term.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter20.E2.80.9322_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter20.E2.80.9322-74"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> In fact, other than Blaine, the only Republican boss initially nominated was Redfield Proctor, as Secretary of War. Senator Shelby Cullom's comment symbolizes Harrison's steadfast aversion to use federal positions for patronage: "I suppose Harrison treated me as well as he did any other Senator; but whenever he did anything for me, it was done so ungraciously that the concession tended to anger rather than please."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter33_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter33-75"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison's selections shared particular alliances – such as their service in the Civil War, Indiana citizenship and membership in the Presbyterian Church.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter20_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter20-76"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Nevertheless, Harrison with these choices had alienated pivotal Republican operatives from New York to Pennsylvania to Iowa and prematurely compromised his political power and future.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter22.E2.80.9330_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter22.E2.80.9330-77"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison's normal schedule provided for two full cabinet meetings per week, as well as separate weekly one-on-one meetings with each cabinet member.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter85_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter85-78"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_service_reform_and_pensions">Civil service reform and pensions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Civil service reform and pensions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harrison_Football_Political_Cartoon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/42/Harrison_Football_Political_Cartoon.jpg/250px-Harrison_Football_Political_Cartoon.jpg" width="250" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/42/Harrison_Football_Political_Cartoon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/42/Harrison_Football_Political_Cartoon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="358" data-file-height="222" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harrison_Football_Political_Cartoon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Political_football" title="Political football">Political football</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Civil_service" title="Civil service">Civil service</a> reform was a prominent issue following Harrison's election. Harrison had campaigned as a supporter of the <a href="/wiki/Merit_system" title="Merit system">merit system</a>, as opposed to the <a href="/wiki/Spoils_system" title="Spoils system">spoils system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter32_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter32-79"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Although some of the civil service had been classified under the <a href="/wiki/Pendleton_Civil_Service_Reform_Act" title="Pendleton Civil Service Reform Act">Pendleton Act</a> by previous administrations, Harrison spent much of his first months in office deciding on political appointments.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter32.E2.80.9336_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter32.E2.80.9336-80"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> Congress was widely divided on the issue and Harrison was reluctant to address the issue in hope of preventing the alienation of either side. The issue became a <a href="/wiki/Political_football" title="Political football">political football</a> of the time and was immortalized in a cartoon captioned "What can I do when both parties insist on kicking?"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale83.2C_86_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale83.2C_86-81"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison appointed <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Smith_Thompson" title="Hugh Smith Thompson">Hugh Smith Thompson</a>, both reformers, to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Civil_Service_Commission" title="United States Civil Service Commission">Civil Service Commission</a>, but otherwise did little to further the reform cause.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter39.E2.80.9341_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter39.E2.80.9341-82"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Harrison quickly saw the enactment of the <a href="/wiki/Dependent_and_Disability_Pension_Act" title="Dependent and Disability Pension Act">Dependent and Disability Pension Act</a> in 1890, a cause he had championed while in Congress.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter36.E2.80.9337Calhoun72.E2.80.9373_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter36.E2.80.9337Calhoun72.E2.80.9373-83"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to providing pensions to disabled Civil War veterans (regardless of the cause of their disability), the Act depleted some of the troublesome federal budget surplus.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter36.E2.80.9337Calhoun72.E2.80.9373_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter36.E2.80.9337Calhoun72.E2.80.9373-83"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> Pension expenditures reached $135&#160;million under Harrison, the largest expenditure of its kind to that point in American history, a problem exacerbated by <a href="/wiki/Pension_Bureau" title="Pension Bureau" class="mw-redirect">Pension Bureau</a> commissioner <a href="/wiki/James_R._Tanner" title="James R. Tanner">James R. Tanner</a>'s expansive interpretation of the pension laws.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter36.E2.80.9337Calhoun72.E2.80.9373_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter36.E2.80.9337Calhoun72.E2.80.9373-83"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison, who privately believed that appointing Tanner had been a mistake, due to his apparent loose management style and tongue, asked Tanner to resign and replaced him with <a href="/wiki/Green_Berry_Raum" title="Green Berry Raum">Green B. Raum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter34.E2.80.9336_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter34.E2.80.9336-84"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Raum was also accused of accepting loan payments in return for expediting pension cases.<sup id="cite_ref-Woodward-Williams_pp193-194_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Woodward-Williams_pp193-194-85"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison, having accepted a dissenting Congressional Republican investigation report that exonerated Raum, kept him in office for the rest of his administration.<sup id="cite_ref-Woodward-Williams_pp193-194_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Woodward-Williams_pp193-194-85"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>One of the first appointments Harrison was forced to reverse was that of James S. Clarkson as an assistant postmaster. Clarkson, who had expected a full cabinet position, began sabotaging the appointment from the outset, gaining the reputation for "decapitating a fourth class postmaster every three minutes". Clarkson himself stated, I am simply on detail from the Republican Committee...I am most anxious to get through this task and leave." He resigned in September 1890.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter34.E2.80.9336_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter34.E2.80.9336-84"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tariff">Tariff</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Tariff">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Billion_dollar_Congress.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Billion_dollar_Congress.jpg/150px-Billion_dollar_Congress.jpg" width="150" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Billion_dollar_Congress.jpg/225px-Billion_dollar_Congress.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Billion_dollar_Congress.jpg/300px-Billion_dollar_Congress.jpg 2x" data-file-width="623" data-file-height="685" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Billion_dollar_Congress.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Harrison and the <a href="/wiki/51st_United_States_Congress" title="51st United States Congress">Billion-Dollar Congress</a> are portrayed as wasting the surplus in this cartoon from <i><a href="/wiki/Puck_(magazine)" title="Puck (magazine)">Puck</a></i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariff</a> levels had been a major political issue since before the Civil War, and they became the most dominant matter of the 1888 election.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter51_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter51-86"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> The high tariff rates had created a surplus of money in the Treasury, which led many Democrats (as well as the growing Populist movement) to call for lowering them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter49_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter49-87"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> Most Republicans preferred to maintain the rates, spend the surplus on <a href="/wiki/Public_works" title="Public works">internal improvements</a> and eliminate some internal taxes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter49_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter49-87"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Representative <a href="/wiki/William_McKinley" title="William McKinley">William McKinley</a> and Senator <a href="/wiki/Nelson_W._Aldrich" title="Nelson W. Aldrich">Nelson W. Aldrich</a> framed the <a href="/wiki/McKinley_Tariff" title="McKinley Tariff">McKinley Tariff</a> that would raise the tariff even higher, including making some rates intentionally prohibitive.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun100.E2.80.93104Socolofsky_.26_Spetter51.E2.80.9352_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun100.E2.80.93104Socolofsky_.26_Spetter51.E2.80.9352-88"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> At Secretary of State James Blaine's urging, Harrison attempted to make the tariff more acceptable by urging Congress to add <a href="/wiki/Reciprocity_(international_relations)" title="Reciprocity (international relations)">reciprocity</a> provisions, which would allow the President to reduce rates when other countries reduced their rates on American exports.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter51_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter51-86"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> The tariff was removed from imported raw <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a>, and sugar growers in the United States were given a two cent per pound subsidy on their production.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun100.E2.80.93104Socolofsky_.26_Spetter51.E2.80.9352_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun100.E2.80.93104Socolofsky_.26_Spetter51.E2.80.9352-88"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> Even with the reductions and reciprocity, the McKinley Tariff enacted the highest average rate in American history, and the spending associated with it contributed to the reputation of the <a href="/wiki/51st_United_States_Congress" title="51st United States Congress">Billion-Dollar Congress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter51_86-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter51-86"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antitrust_laws_and_the_currency">Antitrust laws and the currency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Antitrust laws and the currency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John-Sherman-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/John-Sherman-2.jpg/170px-John-Sherman-2.jpg" width="170" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/John-Sherman-2.jpg/255px-John-Sherman-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/John-Sherman-2.jpg/340px-John-Sherman-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="406" data-file-height="489" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John-Sherman-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Senator <a href="/wiki/John_Sherman" title="John Sherman">John Sherman</a> worked closely with Harrison, writing bills regulating <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Antitrust_Act" title="Sherman Antitrust Act">monopolies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Silver_Purchase_Act" title="Sherman Silver Purchase Act">monetary policy</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Members of both parties were concerned with the growth of the power of <a href="/wiki/Trust_(19th_century)" title="Trust (19th century)" class="mw-redirect">trusts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monopoly" title="Monopoly">monopolies</a>, and one of the first acts of the <a href="/wiki/51st_United_States_Congress" title="51st United States Congress">51st Congress</a> was to pass the <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Antitrust_Act" title="Sherman Antitrust Act">Sherman Antitrust Act</a>, sponsored by Senator <a href="/wiki/John_Sherman" title="John Sherman">John Sherman</a> of Ohio.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter53_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter53-89"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> The Act passed by wide margins in both houses, and Harrison signed it into law.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter53_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter53-89"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> The Sherman Act was the first Federal act of its kind, and marked a new use of federal government power.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun92.E2.80.9393_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun92.E2.80.9393-90"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> While Harrison approved of the law and its intent, his administration was not particularly vigorous in enforcing it.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter54Calhoun94_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter54Calhoun94-91"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the government successfully concluded a case during Harrison's time in office (against a Tennessee coal company),<sup id="cite_ref-coal_case_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coal_case-92"><span>[</span>d<span>]</span></a></sup> and had initiated several other cases against trusts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter54Calhoun94_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter54Calhoun94-91"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>One of the most volatile questions of the 1880s was whether the currency should be backed by <a href="/wiki/Bimetallism" title="Bimetallism">gold and silver</a>, or by <a href="/wiki/Gold_standard" title="Gold standard">gold alone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun94.E2.80.9395_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun94.E2.80.9395-93"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> The issue cut across party lines, with western Republicans and southern Democrats joining together in the call for the free coinage of silver, and both parties' representatives in the northeast holding firm for the gold standard.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun94.E2.80.9395Socolofsky_.26_Spetter55.E2.80.9359_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun94.E2.80.9395Socolofsky_.26_Spetter55.E2.80.9359-94"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> Because silver was worth less than its legal equivalent in gold, taxpayers paid their government bills in silver, while international creditors demanded payment in gold, resulting in a depletion of the nation's gold supply.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun94.E2.80.9395Socolofsky_.26_Spetter55.E2.80.9359_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun94.E2.80.9395Socolofsky_.26_Spetter55.E2.80.9359-94"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> Owing to worldwide <a href="/wiki/Deflation" title="Deflation">deflation</a> in the late 19th century, however, a strict gold standard had resulted in reduction of incomes without the equivalent reduction in debts, pushing debtors and the poor to call for silver coinage as an inflationary measure.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun94.E2.80.9395Socolofsky_.26_Spetter55.E2.80.9359_94-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun94.E2.80.9395Socolofsky_.26_Spetter55.E2.80.9359-94"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The silver coinage issue had not been much discussed in the 1888 campaign and Harrison is said to have favored a bimetallist position.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter53_89-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter53-89"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> However, his appointment of a silverite Treasury Secretary, <a href="/wiki/William_Windom" title="William Windom">William Windom</a>, encouraged the free silver supporters.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter56.E2.80.9357_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter56.E2.80.9357-95"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison attempted to steer a middle course between the two positions, advocating a free coinage of silver, but at its own value, not at a fixed ratio to gold.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter58Calhoun96_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter58Calhoun96-96"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> This failed to facilitate a compromise between the factions. In July 1890, Senator Sherman achieved passage of a bill, the <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Silver_Purchase_Act" title="Sherman Silver Purchase Act">Sherman Silver Purchase Act</a>, in both houses.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter58Calhoun96_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter58Calhoun96-96"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison thought that the bill would end the controversy, and he signed it into law.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter59_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter59-97"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> The effect of the bill, however, was the increased depletion of the nation's gold supply, a problem that would persist until the second Cleveland administration <a href="/wiki/Grover_Cleveland#Economic_panic_and_the_silver_issue" title="Grover Cleveland">resolved it</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter60_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter60-98"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_rights">Civil rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Civil rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Benjamin_Harrison_on_ship.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/President_Benjamin_Harrison_on_ship.jpg/220px-President_Benjamin_Harrison_on_ship.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/President_Benjamin_Harrison_on_ship.jpg/330px-President_Benjamin_Harrison_on_ship.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/President_Benjamin_Harrison_on_ship.jpg/440px-President_Benjamin_Harrison_on_ship.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1180" data-file-height="842" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Benjamin_Harrison_on_ship.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Harrison with Secretary Blaine and Representative <a href="/wiki/Henry_Cabot_Lodge" title="Henry Cabot Lodge">Henry Cabot Lodge</a> off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a>, 1889</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After regaining the majority in both Houses of Congress, some Republicans, led by Harrison, attempted to pass legislation to protect black Americans' civil rights.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun89.E2.80.9390_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun89.E2.80.9390-99"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison's Attorney General, <a href="/wiki/William_H._H._Miller" title="William H. H. Miller">William H. H. Miller</a>, through the Justice Department, ordered the prosecutions for violation of voting rights in the South; however, white juries often failed to convict or indict violators.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun89.E2.80.9390_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun89.E2.80.9390-99"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> This prompted Harrison to urge Congress to pass legislation that would "secure all our people a free exercise of the right of suffrage and every other civil right under the Constitution and laws."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun89.E2.80.9390_99-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun89.E2.80.9390-99"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison endorsed the proposed <a href="/wiki/Lodge_Bill" title="Lodge Bill">Federal Elections Bill</a> written by Representative <a href="/wiki/Henry_Cabot_Lodge" title="Henry Cabot Lodge">Henry Cabot Lodge</a> and Senator <a href="/wiki/George_Frisbie_Hoar" title="George Frisbie Hoar">George Frisbie Hoar</a> in 1890, but the bill was defeated in the Senate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilson32.E2.80.9333_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilson32.E2.80.9333-100"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Following the failure to pass the bill, Harrison continued to speak in favor of <a href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">African American</a> civil rights in addresses to Congress. Most notably, on December 3, 1889, Harrison had gone before Congress and stated:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>The colored people did not intrude themselves upon us; they were brought here in chains and held in communities where they are now chiefly bound by a cruel slave code...when and under what conditions is the black man to have a free ballot? When is he in fact to have those full civil rights which have so long been his in law? When is that quality of influence which our form of government was intended to secure to the electors to be restored? ... in many parts of our country where the colored population is large the people of that race are by various devices deprived of any effective exercise of their political rights and of many of their civil rights. The wrong does not expend itself upon those whose votes are suppressed. Every constituency in the Union is wronged.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter62_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter62-101"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>He severely questioned the states' civil rights records, arguing that if states have the authority over civil rights, then "we have a right to ask whether they are at work upon it."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilson32.E2.80.9333_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilson32.E2.80.9333-100"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison also supported a bill proposed by Senator <a href="/wiki/Henry_W._Blair" title="Henry W. Blair">Henry W.
