Blair</a>, which would have granted federal funding to schools regardless of the students' races.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter65.E2.80.9367_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter65.E2.80.9367-102"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> He also endorsed a proposed constitutional amendment to overturn the Supreme Court ruling in the <i><a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Cases" title="Civil Rights Cases">Civil Rights Cases</a></i> (1883) that declared much of the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1875" title="Civil Rights Act of 1875">Civil Rights Act of 1875</a> unconstitutional.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun89.E2.80.9390Smith170_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun89.E2.80.9390Smith170-103"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> None of these measures gained congressional approval.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun89.E2.80.9390Smith170_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun89.E2.80.9390Smith170-103"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_forests">National forests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: National forests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March 1891 Congress enacted and Harrison signed the <a href="/wiki/Land_Revision_Act_of_1891" title="Land Revision Act of 1891">Land Revision Act of 1891</a>. This legislation resulted from a bipartisan desire to initiate <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">reclamation</a> of surplus lands that had been, up to that point, granted from the public domain, for potential settlement or use by railroad syndicates. As the law's drafting was finalized, Section 24 was added at the behest of Harrison by his Secretary of the Interior John Noble, which read as follows:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>That the President of the United States may, from time to time, set apart and reserve, in any State or Territory having public land bearing forests, in any part of the public lands wholly or in part covered with timber or undergrowth, whether of commercial value or not, as public reservations, and the President shall, by public proclamation, declare the establishment of such reservations and the limits thereof.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter71_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter71-104"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Within a month of the enactment of this law Harrison authorized the first forest reserve, to be located on public domain adjacent to Yellowstone Park, in Wyoming. Other areas were so designated by Harrison, bringing the first forest reservations total to 22 million acres in his term.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter72_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter72-105"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Native_American_policy">Native American policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Native American policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During Harrison's administration, the <a href="/wiki/Lakota_Sioux" title="Lakota Sioux" class="mw-redirect">Lakota Sioux</a>, previously confined to reservations in South Dakota, grew restive under the influence of <a href="/wiki/Wovoka" title="Wovoka">Wovoka</a>, a medicine man, who encouraged them to participate in a spiritual movement called the <a href="/wiki/Ghost_Dance" title="Ghost Dance">Ghost Dance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter106_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter106-106"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> Many in Washington did not understand the predominantly religious nature of the Ghost Dance, and thought it was a militant movement being used to rally Native Americans against the government. On December 29, 1890, troops from the <a href="/wiki/7th_Cavalry_Regiment_(United_States)" title="7th Cavalry Regiment (United States)" class="mw-redirect">Seventh Cavalry</a> clashed with the Sioux at <a href="/wiki/Wounded_Knee_Massacre" title="Wounded Knee Massacre">Wounded Knee</a>. The result was a massacre of at least 146 Sioux, including many women and children;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale121.E2.80.93122Socolofsky_.26_Spetter106.E2.80.93107_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale121.E2.80.93122Socolofsky_.26_Spetter106.E2.80.93107-107"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> the dead Sioux were buried in a mass grave.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale121_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale121-108"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> In reaction Harrison directed Major General <a href="/wiki/Nelson_A._Miles" title="Nelson A. Miles">Nelson A. Miles</a> to investigate and ordered 3500 federal troops to South Dakota; the uprising was brought to an end.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter106_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter106-106"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> Wounded Knee is considered the last major American Indian battle in the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale121.E2.80.93122_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale121.E2.80.93122-109"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison's general policy on American Indians was to encourage assimilation into white society and, despite the massacre, he believed the policy to have been generally successful.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter92_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter92-110"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> This policy, known as the <a href="/wiki/Allotment_Era" title="Allotment Era" class="mw-redirect">allotment system</a> and embodied in the <a href="/wiki/Dawes_Severalty_Act" title="Dawes Severalty Act" class="mw-redirect">Dawes Act</a>, was favored by liberal reformers at the time, but eventually proved detrimental to American Indians as they sold most of their land at low prices to white speculators.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun112.E2.80.93114Stuart452.E2.80.93454_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun112.E2.80.93114Stuart452.E2.80.93454-111"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology_and_naval_modernization">Technology and naval modernization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Technology and naval modernization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USS_Texas2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/USS_Texas2.jpg/250px-USS_Texas2.jpg" width="250" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/USS_Texas2.jpg/375px-USS_Texas2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/USS_Texas2.jpg/500px-USS_Texas2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7147" data-file-height="5290" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USS_Texas2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/USS_Texas_(1892)" title="USS Texas (1892)">USS&#160;<i>Texas</i></a>, America's first battleship, built in 1892</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Harrison's time in office, the United States was continuing to experience advances in science and technology. Harrison was the earliest President whose voice is known to be preserved. That <span class="unicode haudio" style="white-space:nowrap;"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/File:Benjamin_Harrison_speech.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160; <a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/95/Benjamin_Harrison_speech.ogg" class="internal" title="Benjamin Harrison speech.ogg">thirty-six-second recording</a></span>&#160;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Benjamin_Harrison_speech.ogg" title="File:Benjamin Harrison speech.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span> was originally made on a wax <a href="/wiki/Phonograph_cylinder" title="Phonograph cylinder">phonograph cylinder</a> in 1889 by <a href="/wiki/Gianni_Bettini" title="Gianni Bettini">Gianni Bettini</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vincent_Voice_Library_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vincent_Voice_Library-112"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison also had electricity installed in the White House for the first time by <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">Edison General Electric Company</a>, but he and his wife would not touch the light switches for fear of electrocution and would often go to sleep with the lights on.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale96_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale96-113"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Over the course of his administration Harrison marshaled the country's technology to clothe the nation with a credible naval power. When he took office there were only two commissioned warships in the Navy. In his inaugural address he said, "construction of a sufficient number of warships and their necessary armaments should progress as rapidly as is consistent with care and perfection."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter97_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter97-114"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison's Secretary of the Navy Benjamin F. Tracy spearheaded the rapid construction of vessels, and within a year congressional approval was obtained for building of the warships <a href="/wiki/USS_Indiana_(BB-1)" title="USS Indiana (BB-1)"><i>Indiana</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Texas_(1892)" title="USS Texas (1892)"><i>Texas</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Oregon_(BB-3)" title="USS Oregon (BB-3)"><i>Oregon</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/USS_Columbia_(C-12)" title="USS Columbia (C-12)"><i>Columbia</i></a>. By 1898, with the help of the Carnegie Corporation, no less than ten modern warships, including steel hulls and greater displacements and armaments, had transformed the United States into a legitimate naval power. Seven of these had begun during the Harrison term.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter102_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter102-115"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_policy">Foreign policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Foreign policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_America_and_Samoa">Latin America and Samoa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Latin America and Samoa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Harrison and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a> Blaine were often not the most cordial of friends, but harmonized in an aggressive foreign policy and commercial reciprocity with other nations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun74.E2.80.9376_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun74.E2.80.9376-116"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Blaine's persistent medical problems warranted more of a hands-on effort by Harrison in the conduct of foreign policy. In <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, while on tour of the United States in 1891, Harrison proclaimed that the United States was in a "new epoch" of trade and that the expanding navy would protect oceanic shipping and increase American influence and prestige abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun119.E2.80.93121_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun119.E2.80.93121-117"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/First_International_Conference_of_American_States" title="First International Conference of American States">First International Conference of American States</a> met in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington</a> in 1889; Harrison set an aggressive agenda including customs and currency integration and named a bipartisan delegation to the conference, led by <a href="/wiki/John_B._Henderson" title="John B. Henderson">John B. Henderson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie" title="Andrew Carnegie">Andrew Carnegie</a>. The conference failed to achieve any diplomatic breakthrough, due in large part to an atmosphere of suspicion fostered by the Argentinian delegation. It did succeed in establishing an information center that became the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Pan American Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale108_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale108-118"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> In response to the diplomatic bust, Harrison and Blaine pivoted diplomatically and initiated a crusade for tariff reciprocity with Latin American nations; the Harrison administration concluded eight reciprocity treaties among these countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter117.E2.80.93120_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter117.E2.80.93120-119"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> On another front, Harrison sent <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a> as ambassador to <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, but failed in his attempts to establish a naval base there.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter126.E2.80.93128_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter126.E2.80.93128-120"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1889, the United States, the United Kingdom and Germany were locked in a dispute over control of the Samoan Islands. Historian George H. Ryden's research indicates Harrison played a key role in determining the status of this Pacific outpost by taking a firm stand on every aspect of Samoa conference negotiations; this included selection of the local ruler, refusal to allow an indemnity for Germany, as well as the establishment of a three power protectorate, a first for the U.S.. These arrangements facilitated the future dominant power of the U.S. in the Pacific; Secretary of State Blaine was absent due to complication of lumbago.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter115.E2.80.93116_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter115.E2.80.93116-121"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_embargo_of_U.S._pork">European embargo of U.S. pork</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: European embargo of U.S. pork">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Throughout the 1880s various European countries had imposed a ban on importation of United States pork out of an unconfirmed concern of <a href="/wiki/Trichinosis" title="Trichinosis">trichinosis</a>; at issue was over one billion pounds of pork products with a value of $80 million (annually). Harrison engaged Whitelaw Reid, minister to France, and <a href="/wiki/William_Walter_Phelps" title="William Walter Phelps">William Walter Phelps</a>, minister to Germany, to restore these exports for the country without delay. Harrison also successfully asked the congress to enact the Meat Inspection Act to eliminate the accusations of product compromise. The president also partnered with Agriculture Secretary Rusk to threaten Germany with retaliation – by initiating an embargo in the U.S. against Germany's highly demanded beet sugar. By September 1891 Germany relented, and was soon followed by Denmark, France and Austria-Hungary.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter131.E2.80.93136_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter131.E2.80.93136-122"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Crises_in_Aleutian_Islands_and_Chile">Crises in Aleutian Islands and Chile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Crises in Aleutian Islands and Chile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The first international crisis Harrison faced arose from disputed fishing rights on the <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaskan</a> coast. <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> claimed fishing and <a href="/wiki/Seal_hunting" title="Seal hunting">sealing</a> rights around many of the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a>, in violation of U.S. law.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter137.E2.80.93138_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter137.E2.80.93138-123"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> As a result, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> seized several Canadian ships.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter137.E2.80.93138_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter137.E2.80.93138-123"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1891, the administration began negotiations with the British that would eventually lead to a compromise over fishing rights after international arbitration, with the British government paying compensation in 1898<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale135.E2.80.93136Socolofsky_.26_Spetter139.E2.80.93143_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale135.E2.80.93136Socolofsky_.26_Spetter139.E2.80.93143-124"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1891, a diplomatic crisis emerged in <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, otherwise known as the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Crisis" title="Baltimore Crisis" class="mw-redirect"><i>Baltimore</i> Crisis</a>. The American minister to Chile, <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Egan_(land_reformer_and_diplomat)" title="Patrick Egan (land reformer and diplomat)">Patrick Egan</a>, granted asylum to Chileans who were seeking refuge during the <a href="/wiki/1891_Chilean_Civil_War" title="1891 Chilean Civil War" class="mw-redirect">1891 Chilean Civil War</a>. Egan, previously a militant Irish immigrant to the U.S., was motivated by a personal desire to thwart Great Britain's influence in Chile;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter146_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter146-125"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> his action increased tensions between Chile and the United States, which began in the early 1880s when Secretary Blaine had alienated the Chileans in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">War of the Pacific</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Uss_baltimore_c-3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Uss_baltimore_c-3.jpg/300px-Uss_baltimore_c-3.jpg" width="300" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Uss_baltimore_c-3.jpg/450px-Uss_baltimore_c-3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Uss_baltimore_c-3.jpg/600px-Uss_baltimore_c-3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="740" data-file-height="391" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Uss_baltimore_c-3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Attack on sailors from the <a href="/wiki/USS_Baltimore_(C-3)" title="USS Baltimore (C-3)">USS <i>Baltimore</i></a> spawned the 1891 Chilean crisis.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The crisis began in earnest when sailors from the <a href="/wiki/USS_Baltimore_(C-3)" title="USS Baltimore (C-3)">USS&#160;<i>Baltimore</i></a> took <a href="/wiki/Shore_leave" title="Shore leave">shore leave</a> in <a href="/wiki/Valparaiso" title="Valparaiso" class="mw-redirect">Valparaiso</a> and a fight ensued, resulting in the deaths of two American sailors and the arrest of three dozen others.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun127_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun127-126"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i>Baltimore's</i> captain, Winfield Schley, based on the nature of the sailors' wounds, insisted the sailors had been bayonet-attacked by Chilean police without provocation. With Blaine incapacitated, Harrison drafted a demand for reparations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun128.E2.80.93129Socolofsky_.26_Spetter147.E2.80.93149_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun128.E2.80.93129Socolofsky_.26_Spetter147.E2.80.93149-127"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> The Chilean Minister of Foreign Affairs Manuel Matta replied that Harrison's message was "erroneous or deliberately incorrect," and said that the Chilean government was treating the affair the same as any other criminal matter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun128.E2.80.93129Socolofsky_.26_Spetter147.E2.80.93149_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun128.E2.80.93129Socolofsky_.26_Spetter147.E2.80.93149-127"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Tensions increased to the brink of war – Harrison threatened to break off diplomatic relations unless the United States received a suitable apology, and said the situation required, "grave and patriotic consideration". The president also remarked, "If the dignity as well as the prestige and influence of the United States are not to be wholly sacrificed, we must protect those who in foreign ports display the flag or wear the colors."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter151_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter151-128"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> The Navy was also placed on a high level of preparedness. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun128.E2.80.93129Socolofsky_.26_Spetter147.E2.80.93149_127-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun128.E2.80.93129Socolofsky_.26_Spetter147.E2.80.93149-127"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> A recuperated Blaine made brief conciliatory overtures to the Chilean government which had no support in the administration; he then reversed course, joined the chorus for unconditional concessions and apology by the Chileans, who ultimately obliged, and war was averted. Theodore Roosevelt later applauded Harrison for his use of the "big stick" in the matter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale134_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale134-129"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter150.E2.80.93151_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter150.E2.80.93151-130"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Annexation_of_Hawaii">Annexation of Hawaii</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Annexation of Hawaii">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the last days of his administration, Harrison dealt with the issue of <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaiian</a> annexation. Following <a href="/wiki/Overthrow_of_the_Kingdom_of_Hawaii" title="Overthrow of the Kingdom of Hawaii">a coup d'état</a> against Queen <a href="/wiki/Liliuokalani" title="Liliuokalani">Liliuokalani</a>, the new government of Hawaii led by <a href="/wiki/Sanford_B._Dole" title="Sanford B. Dole">Sanford Dole</a> petitioned for annexation by the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter204.E2.80.93205_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter204.E2.80.93205-131"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison was interested in expanding American influence in Hawaii and in establishing a naval base at <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor" title="Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a> but had not previously expressed an opinion on annexing the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun125.E2.80.93126_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun125.E2.80.93126-132"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> The United States <a href="/wiki/Consul_(representative)" title="Consul (representative)">consul</a> in Hawaii <a href="/wiki/John_L._Stevens" title="John L. Stevens">John L. Stevens</a> recognized the new government on February 1, 1893 and forwarded their proposals to Washington. With just one month left before leaving office, the administration signed a treaty on February 14 and submitted it to the Senate the next day with Harrison's recommendation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter204.E2.80.93205_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter204.E2.80.93205-131"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> The Senate failed to act, and President Cleveland withdrew the treaty shortly after taking office.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun132Moore_.26_Hale147_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun132Moore_.26_Hale147-133"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cabinet">Cabinet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Cabinet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BHarrison_cabinet.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/BHarrison_cabinet.jpg/350px-BHarrison_cabinet.jpg" width="350" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/BHarrison_cabinet.jpg/525px-BHarrison_cabinet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/BHarrison_cabinet.jpg/700px-BHarrison_cabinet.jpg 2x" data-file-width="756" data-file-height="588" /></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_appointments">Judicial appointments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Judicial appointments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Harrison_judicial_appointments" title="Benjamin Harrison judicial appointments" class="mw-redirect">Benjamin Harrison judicial appointments</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Supreme_Court">Supreme Court</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Supreme Court">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DavidBrewer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/DavidBrewer.jpg/170px-DavidBrewer.jpg" width="170" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/DavidBrewer.jpg/255px-DavidBrewer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/DavidBrewer.jpg/340px-DavidBrewer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="483" data-file-height="640" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DavidBrewer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Harrison appointed four Supreme Court justices, including <a href="/wiki/David_Josiah_Brewer" title="David Josiah Brewer">David Josiah Brewer</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Harrison appointed four justices to the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a>. The first was <a href="/wiki/David_Josiah_Brewer" title="David Josiah Brewer">David Josiah Brewer</a>, a judge on the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Eighth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Eighth Circuit">Court of Appeals for the Eighth Circuit</a>. Brewer, the nephew of Justice <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Johnson_Field" title="Stephen Johnson Field">Field</a>, had previously been considered for a cabinet position.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter188.E2.80.93190_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter188.E2.80.93190-134"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> Shortly after Brewer's nomination, Justice <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Matthews_(lawyer)" title="Stanley Matthews (lawyer)">Matthews</a> died, creating another vacancy. Harrison had considered <a href="/wiki/Henry_Billings_Brown" title="Henry Billings Brown">Henry Billings Brown</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a> judge and <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_law" title="Admiralty law">admiralty law</a> expert, for the first vacancy and now nominated him for the second.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter188.E2.80.93190_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter188.E2.80.93190-134"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> For the third vacancy, which arose in 1892, Harrison nominated <a href="/wiki/George_Shiras,_Jr." title="George Shiras, Jr.">George Shiras</a>. Shiras's appointment was somewhat controversial because his age—sixty—was older than usual for a newly appointed Justice.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter188.E2.80.93190_134-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter188.E2.80.93190-134"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> Shiras also drew the opposition of Senator <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Quay" title="Matthew Quay">Matthew Quay</a> of Pennsylvania because they were in different factions of the Pennsylvania Republican party, but his nomination was nonetheless approved.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter188.E2.80.93190_134-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter188.E2.80.93190-134"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> Finally, at the end of his term, Harrison nominated <a href="/wiki/Howell_Edmunds_Jackson" title="Howell Edmunds Jackson">Howell Edmunds Jackson</a> to replace Justice <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Quintus_Cincinnatus_Lamar_(II)" title="Lucius Quintus Cincinnatus Lamar (II)" class="mw-redirect">Lamar</a>, who died in January 1893. Harrison knew the incoming Senate would be controlled by Democrats, so he selected Jackson, a respected Tennessee Democrat with whom he was friendly to ensure his nominee would not be rejected.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter188.E2.80.93190_134-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter188.E2.80.93190-134"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> Jackson's nomination was indeed successful, but he died after only two years on the Court.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter188.E2.80.93190_134-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter188.E2.80.93190-134"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_courts">Other courts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Other courts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In addition to his Supreme Court appointments, Harrison appointed ten judges to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_court_of_appeals" title="United States court of appeals" class="mw-redirect">courts of appeals</a>, two judges to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_circuit_court" title="United States circuit court">circuit courts</a>, and 26 judges to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_district_court" title="United States district court">district courts</a>. Because Harrison was in office when Congress eliminated the circuit courts in favor of the courts of appeals, he and Grover Cleveland were the only two Presidents to have appointed judges to both bodies.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="States_admitted_to_the_Union">States admitted to the Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: States admitted to the Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When Harrison took office, no new states had been admitted in more than a decade, owing to Congressional Democrats' reluctance to admit states that they believed would send Republican members. Early in Harrison's term, however, the <a href="/wiki/Lame_duck_(politics)" title="Lame duck (politics)">lame duck</a> Congress passed bills that admitted four states to the union: <a href="/wiki/North_Dakota" title="North Dakota">North Dakota</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Dakota" title="South Dakota">South Dakota</a> on November 2, 1889, <a href="/wiki/Montana" title="Montana">Montana</a> on November 8, and <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a> on November 11.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter44.E2.80.9345_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter44.E2.80.9345-135"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> The following year two more states held constitutional conventions and were admitted – <a href="/wiki/Idaho" title="Idaho">Idaho</a> on July 3 and <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a> on July 10, 1890.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter44.E2.80.9345_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter44.E2.80.9345-135"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> The initial Congressional delegations from all six states were solidly Republican.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter44.E2.80.9345_135-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter44.E2.80.9345-135"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> More states were admitted under Harrison's presidency than any other since <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a>'s.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vacations_and_travel">Vacations and travel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Vacations and travel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Harrison attended the three-day grand Centennial Celebration of the country in New York City on April 30, 1889. He made the following remarks "We have come into the serious but always inspiring presence of Washington. He was the incarnation of duty and he teaches us today this great lesson: that those who would associate their names with events that shall outlive a century can only do so by high consecration to duty. Self-seeking has no public observance or anniversary."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter160_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter160-136"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Harrisons made many trips out of the capital, which included speeches at most stops – including Philadelphia, New England, Indianapolis and Chicago. The President typically made his best impression speaking before large audiences, as opposed to more intimate settings.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter157_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter157-137"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> The most notable of his presidential trips, theretofore unequaled, was a five-week tour of the west in the spring of 1891, aboard a lavishly outfitted train.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter171_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter171-138"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison quite enjoyed a number of short trips out of the capital, usually for hunting – to nearby Virginia or Maryland. On one such trip the game of choice was coon – for which Harrison was not well experienced – he shot and killed one Gilbert Wooten's hog, having mistaken it for a coon; while Mr. Wooten was thereby made happily famous, the president was not.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter166_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter166-139"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During the dreadfully hot summers of Washington, favorite locations to which the Harrisons made refuge were <a href="/wiki/Deer_Park,_Maryland" title="Deer Park, Maryland">Deer Park, Maryland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_May_Point" title="Cape May Point" class="mw-redirect">Cape May Point</a> in New Jersey. In 1890 John Wanamaker joined with other Philadelphia devotees of the Harrisons and made an entirely unsolicited gift to them of a summer cottage at Cape May. Harrison, though appreciative, was most uncomfortable with the ethical appearance; a month later he wrote Wanamaker a $10,000 personal check for reimbursement to the various donors of the gift. Nevertheless, Harrison's opponents made the gift the subject of national ridicule, in which Mrs. Harrison and the president were both vigorously criticized.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter168_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter168-140"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reelection_campaign_in_1892">Reelection campaign in 1892</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Reelection campaign in 1892">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1892" title="United States presidential election, 1892">United States presidential election, 1892</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eastman_Johnson_-_Benjamin_Harrison_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Eastman_Johnson_-_Benjamin_Harrison_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/170px-Eastman_Johnson_-_Benjamin_Harrison_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Eastman_Johnson_-_Benjamin_Harrison_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/255px-Eastman_Johnson_-_Benjamin_Harrison_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Eastman_Johnson_-_Benjamin_Harrison_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/340px-Eastman_Johnson_-_Benjamin_Harrison_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3502" data-file-height="5271" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eastman_Johnson_-_Benjamin_Harrison_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Official <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> portrait of Benjamin Harrison, painted by <a href="/wiki/Eastman_Johnson" title="Eastman Johnson">Eastman Johnson</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The treasury surplus had evaporated and the nation's economic health was worsening – precursors to the eventual <a href="/wiki/Panic_of_1893" title="Panic of 1893">Panic of 1893</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun107.2C_126.E2.80.93127_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun107.2C_126.E2.80.93127-141"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> Congressional elections in 1890 had gone against the Republicans; and although Harrison had cooperated with Congressional Republicans on legislation, several party leaders withdrew their support for him because of his adamant refusal to give party members the nod in the course of his executive appointments. Specifically, Thomas C. Platt, Mathew S. Quay, Thomas B. Reed and James Clarkson quietly organized the Grievance Committee, the ambition of which was to initiate a dump-Harrison offensive. They solicited the support of Blaine, without effect however, and Harrison in reaction resolved to run for re-election – seemingly forced choose one of two options – "become a candidate or forever wear the name of a political coward".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter81_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter81-142"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>It was clear that Harrison would not be re-nominated unanimously.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun134.E2.80.93137_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun134.E2.80.93137-143"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> Many of Harrison's detractors persisted in pushing for an incapacitated Blaine, though he announced that he was not a candidate in February 1892.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun134.E2.80.93137_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun134.E2.80.93137-143"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> Some party leaders still hoped to draft Blaine into running, and speculation increased when he resigned at the 11th hour as Secretary of State in June.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun138.E2.80.93139_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun138.E2.80.93139-144"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/1892_Republican_National_Convention" title="1892 Republican National Convention">convention</a> in <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">Minneapolis</a>, Harrison prevailed on the first ballot, but encountered significant opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun140.E2.80.93141_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun140.E2.80.93141-145"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Democrats renominated former President Cleveland, making the 1892 election a rematch of the one four years earlier. The tariff revisions of the past four years had made imported goods so expensive that now many voters shifted to the reform position.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun147.E2.80.93150_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun147.E2.80.93150-146"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> Many westerners, traditionally Republican voters, defected to the new <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(United_States)" title="People's Party (United States)">Populist Party</a> candidate, <a href="/wiki/James_B._Weaver" title="James B. Weaver">James Weaver</a>, who promised free silver, generous veterans' pensions, and an <a href="/wiki/Eight-hour_day" title="Eight-hour day">eight-hour work day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun145.E2.80.93147_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun145.E2.80.93147-147"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> The effects of the suppression of the <a href="/wiki/Homestead_Strike" title="Homestead Strike">Homestead Strike</a> rebounded against the Republicans as well, although the federal government did not take action.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun145.E2.80.93147_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun145.E2.80.93147-147"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Harrison's wife Caroline began a critical struggle with <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> earlier in 1892 and two weeks before the election, on October 25, it took her life.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun149_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun149-148"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> Their daughter <a href="/wiki/Mary_Harrison_McKee" title="Mary Harrison McKee">Mary Harrison McKee</a> assumed the role of <a href="/wiki/First_Lady_of_the_United_States" title="First Lady of the United States">First Lady</a> after her mother's death.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun156Moore_.26_Hale143.E2.80.93145_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun156Moore_.26_Hale143.E2.80.93145-149"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> Mrs. Harrison's terminal illness and the fact that both candidates had served in the White House called for a low key campaign, and resulted in neither of the candidates actively campaigning personally.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter198.E2.80.93199_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter198.E2.80.93199-150"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Cleveland ultimately won the election by 277 electoral votes to Harrison's 145, and also won the popular vote by 5,556,918 to 5,176,108; this was the most decisive presidential election in 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-EV_1892_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EV_1892-151"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter199_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetter199-152"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-presidency_and_death">Post-presidency and death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Post-presidency and death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grave_of_President_Benjamin_Harrison_and_his_two_wives_in_Indianapolis,_Indiana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Grave_of_President_Benjamin_Harrison_and_his_two_wives_in_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana.jpg/220px-Grave_of_President_Benjamin_Harrison_and_his_two_wives_in_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Grave_of_President_Benjamin_Harrison_and_his_two_wives_in_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana.jpg/330px-Grave_of_President_Benjamin_Harrison_and_his_two_wives_in_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Grave_of_President_Benjamin_Harrison_and_his_two_wives_in_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana.jpg/440px-Grave_of_President_Benjamin_Harrison_and_his_two_wives_in_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grave_of_President_Benjamin_Harrison_and_his_two_wives_in_Indianapolis,_Indiana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Grave of President Harrison and his two wives in Indianapolis, Indiana</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After he left office, Harrison visited the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Columbian_Exposition" title="World's Columbian Exposition">World's Columbian Exposition</a> in Chicago in June 1893,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale150_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale150-153"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> where the nation's first <a href="/wiki/Commemorative_stamp" title="Commemorative stamp">commemorative postage</a> was introduced, an initiative of his Postmaster General, John Wanamaker. After the Expo, Harrison returned to his home in Indianapolis. Harrison had been elected a companion of the <a href="/wiki/Military_Order_of_the_Loyal_Legion_of_the_United_States" title="Military Order of the Loyal Legion of the United States">Military Order of the Loyal Legion of the United States</a> in 1882, and was elected as commander (president) of the Ohio Commandery on May 3, 1893.</p>
<p>For a few months in 1894, Harrison lived in San Francisco, California, where he gave law lectures at <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun158_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun158-154"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1896 some of Harrison's friends in the Republican party tried to convince him to seek the presidency again, but he declined. He traveled around the nation making appearances and speeches in support of William McKinley's candidacy for president.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun160.E2.80.93161_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun160.E2.80.93161-155"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>From July 1895 to March 1901 Harrison served on the Board of Trustees of <a href="/wiki/Purdue_University" title="Purdue University">Purdue University</a>, where Harrison Hall, a dormitory, was named in his honor.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale150_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale150-153"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> He wrote a series of articles about the Federal government and the presidency which were republished in 1897 as a book titled <i>This Country of Ours</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Harrison_1897_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harrison_1897-156"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1899 Harrison attended the <a href="/wiki/Hague_Convention_of_1899" title="Hague Convention of 1899" class="mw-redirect">First Peace Conference</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>.</p>
<p>In 1896, Harrison at age 62 remarried, to <a href="/wiki/Mary_Dimmick_Harrison" title="Mary Dimmick Harrison">Mary Scott Lord Dimmick</a>, the widowed 37-year- old niece and former secretary of his deceased wife. Harrison's two adult children, Russell, 41 years old at the time, and Mary (Mamie) McKee, 38, disapproved of the marriage and did not attend the wedding. Benjamin and Mary had one child together, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Harrison_Walker" title="Elizabeth Harrison Walker">Elizabeth</a> (February 21, 1897&#160;– December 26, 1955).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale153_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale153-157"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1900, Harrison served as an attorney for the Republic of Venezuela in their <a href="/wiki/Schomburgk_Line" title="Schomburgk Line" class="mw-redirect">British Guiana boundary dispute</a> with the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale155_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale155-158"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> An international trial was agreed upon; he filed an 800-page brief and traveled to <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> where he spent more than 25 hours in court on their behalf. Although he lost the case, his legal arguments won him international renown.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun160.E2.80.93163_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun160.E2.80.93163-159"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Harrison developed what was thought to be <a href="/wiki/Influenza" title="Influenza">influenza</a> or grippe in February 1901. He was treated with steam vapor inhalation and oxygen, but his condition worsened. He died from <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a> at <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Harrison_Home" title="Benjamin Harrison Home">his home</a> on Wednesday, March 13, 1901, at the age of 67.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison is interred in Indianapolis's <a href="/wiki/Crown_Hill_Cemetery" title="Crown Hill Cemetery">Crown Hill Cemetery</a>, next to Caroline. After her death, Mary Dimmick Harrison was buried next to him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale156_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore_.26_Hale156-161"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_reputation_and_memorials">Historical reputation and memorials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Historical reputation and memorials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Benjamin_Harrison_Memorial_Statue.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f9/Benjamin_Harrison_Memorial_Statue.jpg/220px-Benjamin_Harrison_Memorial_Statue.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f9/Benjamin_Harrison_Memorial_Statue.jpg/330px-Benjamin_Harrison_Memorial_Statue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f9/Benjamin_Harrison_Memorial_Statue.jpg/440px-Benjamin_Harrison_Memorial_Statue.jpg 2x" data-file-width="576" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Benjamin_Harrison_Memorial_Statue.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<b><a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Harrison_(Niehaus)" title="Benjamin Harrison (Niehaus)">Benjamin Harrison Memorial Statue</a></b><br />
<a href="/wiki/Indianapolis,_Indiana" title="Indianapolis, Indiana" class="mw-redirect">Indianapolis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a><br />
Charles Niehaus &amp; Henry Bacon, <i>1908</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Panic_of_1893" title="Panic of 1893">Panic of 1893</a>, Harrison became more popular in retirement.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun6_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun6-162"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> His legacy among historians is scant, and "general accounts of his period inaccurately treat Harrison as a cipher".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetterx_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetterx-163"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> More recently,</p>
<blockquote>
<p>historians have recognized the importance of the Harrison administration—and Harrison himself—in the new foreign policy of the late nineteenth century. The administration faced challenges throughout the hemisphere, in the Pacific, and in relations with the European powers, involvements that would be taken for granted in the twentieth century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetterx_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESocolofsky_.26_Spetterx-163"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Harrison's presidency belongs properly to the 19th century, but he "clearly pointed the way" to the modern presidency that would emerge under <a href="/wiki/William_McKinley" title="William McKinley">William McKinley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun166_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun166-164"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison's reputation for integrity was largely intact after leaving office in 1893.<sup id="cite_ref-Woodward-Williams_p191_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Woodward-Williams_p191-165"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> The bi-partisan <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Anti-Trust_Act" title="Sherman Anti-Trust Act" class="mw-redirect">Sherman Anti-Trust Act</a> signed into law by Harrison remains in effect over 120 years later and was the most important legislation passed by the Fifty-first Congress.<sup id="cite_ref-Batten_2010_p209_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Batten_2010_p209-166"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison's support for <a href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">African American</a> voting rights and education would be the last significant attempts to protect <a href="/wiki/Civil_rights" title="Civil rights" class="mw-redirect">civil rights</a> until the 1930s.<sup id="cite_ref-Batten_2010_p209_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Batten_2010_p209-166"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison's tenacity at foreign policy was emulated by politicians such as <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Batten_2010_p209_166-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Batten_2010_p209-166"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Harrison was memorialized on several postage stamps. The first was a 13-cent stamp issued on November 18, 1902.<sup id="cite_ref-arago_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arago-167"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> The engraved likeness of Harrison was modeled after a photo provided by Harrison's widow.<sup id="cite_ref-arago_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arago-167"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> In all Harrison has been honored on <a href="/wiki/US_Presidents_on_US_postage_stamps#Benjamin_Harrison" title="US Presidents on US postage stamps" class="mw-redirect">six U.S. Postage stamps</a>, more than most other U.S. Presidents. Harrison also was featured on the five-dollar <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_Notes" title="National Bank Notes" class="mw-redirect">National Bank Notes</a> from the third charter period, beginning in 1902.<sup id="cite_ref-Hudgeons_Hudgeons_2000_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hudgeons_Hudgeons_2000-168"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1908, the people of <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis,_Indiana" title="Indianapolis, Indiana" class="mw-redirect">Indianapolis</a> erected the <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Harrison_(Niehaus)" title="Benjamin Harrison (Niehaus)">Benjamin Harrison memorial statue</a>, created by Charles Niehaus and Henry Bacon, in honor of Harrison's lifetime achievements as military leader, U.S. Senator, and President of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-INgov_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INgov-169"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> The statue occupies a site in <a href="/wiki/Indiana_World_War_Memorial_Plaza#University_Park" title="Indiana World War Memorial Plaza">University Park</a> overlooking the <a href="/wiki/Birch_Bayh_Federal_Building_and_United_States_Courthouse" title="Birch Bayh Federal Building and United States Courthouse">Birch Bayh Federal Building and United States Courthouse</a> across New York Avenue.</p>
<p>In 1942, a <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Ship" title="Liberty Ship" class="mw-redirect">Liberty Ship</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/SS_Benjamin_Harrison" title="SS Benjamin Harrison">SS Benjamin Harrison</a></i>, was named in his honor. In 1951, <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Harrison_Home" title="Benjamin Harrison Home">Harrison's home</a> was opened to the public as a library and museum. It had been used as a dormitory for a music school from 1937 to 1950.<sup id="cite_ref-NPS_Benjamin_Harrison_Home_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPS_Benjamin_Harrison_Home-170"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> The house was designated as a <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark" title="National Historic Landmark">National Historic Landmark</a> in 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-Benjamin_Harrison_Presidential_Site_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benjamin_Harrison_Presidential_Site-171"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, a dollar coin with his image, part of the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_$1_Coin_Program" title="Presidential $1 Coin Program">Presidential $1 Coin Program</a>, was issued.<sup id="cite_ref-US_Mint_dollar_coin_schedule_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_Mint_dollar_coin_schedule-172"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Fort_Benjamin_Harrison" title="Fort Benjamin Harrison">Fort Benjamin Harrison</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Lawrence,_Indiana" title="Lawrence, Indiana">Lawrence, Indiana</a>, a northeastern suburb of Indianapolis, was constructed in 1903 to 1908 and named in his honor. The base was closed in 1991 and the site has been redeveloped to include residential neighborhoods, a golf course, and <a href="/wiki/Fort_Harrison_State_Park" title="Fort Harrison State Park">Fort Harrison State Park</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-VIII-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-VIII_2-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Although he was the eighth Benjamin Harrison in his family, Harrison is known simply as Benjamin Harrison, rather than Benjamin Harrison VIII.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Farmer.27s_College-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Farmer.27s_College_9-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The school was later known as Belmont College. After Belmont closed, the campus was transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Military_Institute" title="Ohio Military Institute">Ohio Military Institute</a>, which closed in 1958.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Seventeenth_Amendment-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Seventeenth_Amendment_40-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Before the passage of the <a href="/wiki/Seventeenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Seventeenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">Seventeenth Amendment to the United States Constitution</a>, Senators were elected by state legislatures.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-coal_case-92"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-coal_case_92-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The case was <i>United States v. Jellico Mountain Coal</i>, 46 Fed. 432. June 4, 1891</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
